WELL EVALUATION
WELL EVALUATION
Oxy USA, Inc.
State Gresz 5-26-35H-143-98
Figure 1. Nabors X-18 at the Oxy USA, Inc. State Gresz 5-26-35H-143-98 well on October 22, 2014; 6 miles northeast of Fairfield in
Billings County, ND. (Photo provided by Laura Godowski, Payzone Geologist)
INTRODUCTION
The Oxy USA, Inc. State Gresz 5-26-35H-143-98
[NENW Sec 26, T143N, R98W] is located
approximately 6 miles northeast of Fairfield, North Dakota. The subject well was drilled in Billings County,
ND by the Nabors X-18 rig in the Hungry Man Butte Field of the Bakken pool. The subject well was
planned with one approximately 9,515' [Intermediate casing to projected total depth (TD)] long southerly
lateral bore with intent to intersect regional hydraulic fracture trends that might enhance reservoir quality
within the Middle Bakken. OXY USA intends to develop oil production in the late Devonian Middle Bakken
target porosity zone with a stratigraphy consisting of siltstone, silty sandstone and limestone with
depositional lithofacies ranging from onshore terrestrial to offshore marine deposits.
ENGINEERING
Surface, Vertical & Curve Operations:
A 13 1/2" surface hole was drilled on October 12, 2014 by Nabors X-18 and surface casing was
set at 2,550'. The vertical hole operations commenced on November 21, 2014 with Baker Hughes
providing equipment and personnel for MWD and directional drilling services.
The first vertical Bottom Hole Assembly (BHA), consisting of MWD tools, 1.50° bend motor and
Tercel MR616M PDC bit, drilled to a depth of 8,452'. At this depth, a trip was made due to a low ROP.
Upon pulling this assembly, a new tool was used with the same make and model bit and an Ultra XL/MS
1.50° motor for the third vertical BHA. This BHA drilled to 9,940' and was pulled out of the hole due to low
ROP. The fourth assembly, a Security MMD55M and an Ultra X-treme Curve motor drilled down to KOP
at 10,473' MD and continued to build the curve to 10,843' MD. This assembly did not produce high
enough build rates and another trip was made at this point.
The fifth assembly, a Tricone Smith bit with the same motor, finished the curve to a planned TD of
11,346' MD and on target of 11,030' TVD. This placed the well bore approximately 11.5' into a 19' thick
(shale to shale) Middle Bakken zone. This 10º/100' curve was drilled in a total circulating hours of 25.6.
However, the total on bottom time for the curve was 19.4 hours.
No E-logs were run due to the close proximity of the State Gresz 4-26-35H-143-98 well.
Directional tools were then pulled out of the hole and a string of 7" intermediate casing was run, set, and
cemented at a depth of 11,331 MD.
After casing operations, a gyro was run to ensure separation
between off-set wells, thus minimizing the ellipse of uncertainty. Once completed, true lateral operations
commenced.
Diesel invert drilling fluid was used throughout the vertical hole and curve build sections
maintaining a 9.8-10 ppg mud weight for stable downhole conditions.
Lateral Operations:
Baker Hughes again provided equipment and personnel for MWD and directional drilling services.
The directional drillers and Payzone geologists worked closely together throughout the project to make
steering decisions in order to maximize the amount of borehole exposure to the pay zone.
A five bladed 6" bit (Security MM54), 1.40º BHI mud motor, and one MWD tool comprised the
lateral BHA (6th BHA overall) and was run in the hole on 4" drill pipe starting at 11,331' MD. This BHA
drilled to a depth of 12,489' MD where the MWD tool failed. The same bit and the same motor was re-run
with a new MWD tool for the seventh BHA drilling to 16,205' MD when the tool failed again. A new
Security bit (MMD54) with a new BHI mud motor was picked up, however, the MWD tool failed when the
tool reached bottom. The ninth BHA was a re-run of the eighth with a new tool and drilled to 18,671' MD
when the motor stopped working. At this point, a new MMD54 Security bit, BHI motor, and MWD tool was
used for the tenth BHA. This tool failed at 18,761', thus another trip was initiated. The same bit and motor
was re-run with a new MWD tool and reached final TD of 20,846' MD.
The lateral was drilled in 10 days in total and spud to TD was a total of 20 days. The lateral
resulted in a TD of 20,846' MD (10,986.87' TVD) at a final azimuth of 173.91º, resulting in a closure
vertical section of 10,021.21. The BHL is located 9,964.61 South & 1,063.59' East of surface location or
approx. 250.61' FSL & 2,803.57 FWL, SE SW Section 35, T143N, R98W (Figure 2).
Salt water drilling fluid was used from the intermediate casing to TD with mud weights throughout
the lateral varying from 9.9-10.2 ppg.

GEOLOGIC EVALUATION
Methods:
Geologic supervision of the well was provided by Payzone Consulting, Inc. with four well site geologists.
Laura Godowski, Kevin Jacks, and Mike Anderson drilled the vertical and curve, and Laura Godowski and
Mike Williamson drilled the horizontal sections. A wireless Totco Gas WatchTM gas chromatograph was
interfaced with a Rigwatch electronic data recorder system and provided total gas, C1, and C3
information for viewing around location through the vertical and curve. Lagged samples were caught in
30' intervals from 8,000' to 11,350' MD and 100' intervals from 11,350' to 20,846' MD (TD). Cuttings were
examined under a binocular microscope and complete lithologic descriptions are provided in the lithology
document within this evaluation. Two sets of dry cuttings were collected, with one set sent to the North
Dakota Geological Survey Core Library and the second set sent to Ed Schirm, the project geologist
overseeing operations.
Lithology and Geologic Interpretation:
Geologic evaluation began at 8,000' within the Minnelusa Formation [Permian; Minnelusa Group] then
the Amsden Formation [Pennsylvanian; Minnelusa Group]. The first top that was used for landing was
the Kibbey "Lime" (within the Kibbey Formation) [Mississippian; Big Snowy Group] which was
penetrated at 8,855' TVD (-6,168.5'). Samples from this interval were described as:
8870-8900 LIMESTONE: mudstone, light gray to gray, light gray to brown, microcrystalline, blocky, firm to hard, anhydrite,
no visible porosity to friable, sandy in part, anhydritic, calcareous cement; trace SILTSTONE: light brown to red, tan, trace
off white to cream, blocky, soft to friable, sandy in part, anhydritic, calcareous cement
The top of the 1st Charles Salt [Mississippian, Madison Group] was penetrated at 9,007' TVD
(-6,320.5'). Within the Charles formation, the Green Point Anhydrite (GP Anhydrite) was penetrated at
9,412' TVD (-6,725.5') and the Base of the Last Charles Salt (BLS) was drilled at 9,498' TVD
(-6,811.5'). Samples from this interval were described as:
9020-9050 SALT: translucent to occasional clear, rare milky, crystalline, subhedral to anhedral, hard
9440-9470 ANHYDRITE: white to off white, cream, amorphous, soft, earthy texture; ARGILLACEOUS LIMESTONE:
wackestone to mudstone, light gray to gray, trace off white, blocky, friable to firm, crystalline texture, anhydritic in part, no
visible porosity; SALT: translucent to occasional clear, rare milky, crystalline, hard, subhedral to anhedral
9500-9530 ARGILLACEOUS LIMESTONE: wackestone to mudstone, light gray to gray, trace off white, blocky, friable to
firm, crystalline texture, dolomitic in part, no visibility porosity
The top of the Mission Canyon Formation [Mississippian; Madison Group] was drilled at 9,686' TVD
(-6,999.5'). The prospective Fryburg interval (within the Mission Canyon Formation) was penetrated at
9,856' TVD (-7,169.5').
The Mission Canyon consisted of interbedded limestone, dolomites, and
anhydrites. Dolomite in the mid to lower Mission Canyon showed fair-moderate intercrystalline porosity to
traces of pinpoint porosity. The samples for this interval were described as:
9710-9740 LIMESTONE: mudstone, tan, gray to light gray, firm, microcrystalline texture, argillaceous in part, no visible
porosity, possible intercrystalline porosity; ANHYDRITE: white, soft, amorphous texture
9860-9890 DOLOMITE LIMESTONE: mudstone, medium brown, light gray, cryptocrystalline, firm, common dead oil
stain, trace sparry calcite, common algal matt, no visibility porosity; DOLOMITE: mudstone, brown, light gray, firm,
common dead oil stain, trace sparry calcite, common algal material
The argillaceous limestone signifying the top of the Lodgepole Formation [Mississippian; Madison
Group] was penetrated at 10,189' TVD (-7,502.5') with 798' TVD of consistent lithology described as:
10220-10250 LIMESTONE: mudstone, gray to light gray, tan to light brown, off white to cream, microcrystalline, firm,
earthy, dolomitic in part, no visibility porosity, possible intercrystalline porosity
The False Bakken (Carrington Shale) within the Lodgepole Formation was drilled at 11,078' MD;
10,987' TVD (-8,300.5'). The False Bakken was described as:
11090-11030 SHALE: medium gray to dark gray, firm to hard, blocky, earthy texture, common disseminated pyrite,
calcareous, no visible porosity
The carbonaceous, petroliferous Upper Bakken Shale signifying the top of the Bakken Formation was
penetrated at 11,144' MD; 11,010' TVD (-8,323.5') and was described as:
11150-11180 SHALE: dark brown, black, soft to occasional friable, blocky, earthy texture, carbonaceous, petroliferous,
common disseminated pyrite; LIMESTONE: as above
The Middle Bakken was penetrated at 11,177' MD; 11,018' TVD (-8,331.5'). The stratigraphy of the
Middle Bakken consisted of varying thicknesses of siltstone, limestone and silty sandstone. (Figure 3 and
4) The packstone bed that occasionally occurs was not present when landing the curve, but pinched back
in at 13,067' MD and was approximately 2-3' thick.
Figure 3. Generalized lithology of the Middle Bakken Member
The Middle Bakken was generally described as:
11350-11400 SILTY SANDSTONE: off white to cream, light gray to gray, light gray brown, very fine grained, friable, sub
rounded to sub angular, calcareous cement, moderately sorted, rare disseminated pyrite, trace intergranular porosity,
possible fracture porosity, trace spotty to even light brown oil stain
Figure 4. Wet cuttings of the Middle Bakken silty sandstone (close-up, left) with main matrix of the in 6-8' target window cuttings of
the Middle Bakken silty sandstone (middle) and with disseminated pyrite (right)*
*All photos: 45x (L. Godowski, Payzone Well site Geologist)

Kick off point for the curve was established from the offset wells' distance of the "base last salt" marker to
the Middle Bakken target zone. The "base last salt to target" approximation suggested a landing target of
11,027' TVD. The landing target was approximated to 11,030' TVD based on the False Bakken pick,
which was encountered at a TVD of 10,987'. The wellbore was landed 11.5' (approximately 11,029.40'
TVD, above center line) below the UBS in the upper half of a 6' thick target zone.
LATERAL GEOLOGY
Gamma Signature:
Within the Middle Bakken silty sandstone/siltstone/limestone target interval, gamma counts varied
between 29 and 130 API. The packstone (20-35 API) was not present when landing the curve. However,
the packstone pinched in when the wellbore approached 13,067' MD. A hotter, dirtier silty
sandstone/siltstone (110-130 API) replaced the limestone in the beginning section of the lateral. The
center of target zone depicted high 40's-mid 60 counts with gamma trending towards the 80's-90's counts
at the top and bottom of the 6' target window. Three hard streaks were encountered in this targeted
interval and located near the top, middle and bottom of target zone. These hard streaks depicted gamma
counts ranging from the mid-50's to the mid-70's API and permitting excellent tracking for the well bore
when in this vicinity.
As the lateral commenced after casing operations, there was excellent control for geo-steering based on
the gamma signature. The packstone that pinched in around 13,000' MD, allowed geologists to infer
where the well bore was in target zone and once encountered, directional was advised to slide down. The
packstone was approximately 2' thick. Below the packstone, a silty sandstone consisted of 60-70's count
gamma which trended into the mid 50's gamma.
This was where the hard streak was encountered
multiple times, permitting the well bore to deflect up. If the inclination was not too severe, the well bore
would then deflect off the packstone and the well bore would track with the "porpoise effect". Once the
well bore was below this hard streak, gamma counts varied from 50-60 API (center of target zone).
Below the center of target, another hard streak was encountered and depicted counts between 68-88
API. Lastly, located at the bottom of target zone was another 85-90's gamma marker which permitted
geologists to consult the directional driller to slide up. This marker occurred at ~14,200'-14,450' MD.
Under this marker, there was no exact confirmation on the thickness to the Lower Bakken Shale, thus
slides up were initiated to avoid any potential shale strikes.
The entire well bore was drilled in between the 19' projected shale to shale zone with excellent gamma
markers and trends that represented the stratigraphy within the lateral. These markers and trends aided
geo-steering tremendously. The wellbore was in the Middle Bakken throughout the entire lateral and 75%
within the 6' targeted interval and 100% within the shale to shale zone.
These gamma markers were used for determining formation dip and depth within the target interval and
permitted efficient geosteering. They are plotted on the Wellsite horizontal log (Figure 6) and dip profile
(Figure 7).
Figure 6
Middle Bakken Zone: Silty Sandstone to Limestone (Packstone)
(Targeted silty sandstone trending into the Packstone)
Siltstone > Silty Sandstone
(Gamma signature for siltstone 95-124 API signature for silty sandstone top of zone 65-80 API Gamma)
Siltstone > Center Target Marker >Packstone
Figure 6. Gamma values (0-120 API scale) depicting stratigraphic marker intervals throughout the target zone.
Geo-steering:
The target zone within the Middle Bakken was established based on the best drill rates, gamma markers
and gas concentrations. A 7' zone of >6% porosity was expected to be encountered in the targeted
interval. Samples from the target zone varied in porosity, oil staining, color, cementation, and pyrite
content. Stratigraphic locations in the target zone were based on drill rates, gas shows, gamma ray
values and sample observations.
The Middle Bakken was penetrated at 11,177' MD; 11,010' TVD and consisted of siltstone and silty
sandstone when landing the curve, the limestone packstone was not seen in the curve although pinched
in later in the well. A 6' target window in an approximately 19' thick Middle Bakken was selected, 8'
above target zone, 6' target zone and 5' underneath.
The wellbore stayed within the 6' targeted interval for approximately 7,140' of 9,515' or 75% of the well
(rat hole out of intermediate casing to TD). The well was drilled in between the 19' shale to shale target
zone for 100% of the lateral. Using the provided offset log information and the structural data provided
from Oxy USA Inc., Payzone geologists were able to anticipate and interpret the dip rate for the well. The
TVD of the formation decreased 39.09' over 9,540' (first survey out of intermediate casing to TD
projection at bit) resulting in an overall up dip of 0.20º or 90.20°.
A total depth of 20,846' was reached on December 11, 2014 at 05:45 MST. Total depth resulted in 100%
overall exposure within the Middle Bakken Member of the Bakken Formation and 75% within the defined
6' targeted interval. (Figure 7)

Hydrocarbons:
During the drilling of the lateral, gas readings were recorded, imported/exported, and analyzed via a
Totco gas detection system. The line was hooked up to the gas sniffer and hard-lined into the base of the
possum belly. Background gas varied significantly from 30-150 units with peaks scattered throughout the
target zone. The highest gas values were encountered when the well bore approached the top of target
zone below the packstone. These elevated backgrounds gases (130-150+units) produced continuous to
intermittent flares that ranged from 2-10' in height. Connection gases reached as high as 160-180 units
with an average of 80-120+ units at connections. Oil show in samples consisted of even to spotty golden
brown oil stain. (Figure 8)

Summary

The Nabors X-18 drilling rig successfully drilled a two-section horizontal wellbore within the
Middle Bakken Member of the Bakken Formation at the OXY USA, Inc. State Gresz 5-26-35H-
143-98.

A mud program consisting of diesel invert (9.9-10.2+ ppg) was used from spud to curve landing
with salt water drilling fluid used from the intermediate casing to 20,846' MD (TD). Salt water
mud (9.7-10.1 ppg) was efficient for maintaining stable down hole conditions and permitted
adequate analysis of gas concentrations in the lateral. Background gas concentrations ranged
from 30-150+ units with connections as high as 160-180 units. These elevated gas levels were
continuous throughout the lateral and the highest concentrations were recorded at the top of the
targeted interval.

Steering was accomplished by sample evaluation and by following correlative drilling rate and
MWD gamma ray markers; making dip estimations based on intersections of these markers with
the well bore. A net of 7,140' (75%) of gross 9,515' of the lateral was drilled in the ideal 6' thick
Middle Bakken target zone with 100% exposure within the 19' shale to shale Middle Bakken
Member of the Bakken Formation.

Samples from the target consisted of white to off-white, light brown, trace light gray, and light gray
to dark gray siltstone/silty sandstone. Traces of intergranular porosity were seen throughout the
lateral. Samples from the ideal zone contained a spotty to even brown oil stain.

The transitional packstone was not present in the landing of the curve and pinched in later in the
lateral section. Three hard streaks were present: one under the packstone, one in the middle of
the target zone and the other at the bottom of the targeted interval. These hard streaks permitted
the well bore to track nicely throughout much of the lateral.

The State Gresz 5-26-35H-143-98 was a successful drilling effort as measured by gross
exposure to the target. The well will be fitted with a 4 ½" production liner and swell packers in
preparation for a fracture stimulation that will determine the true commercial value of the well.
Respectfully submitted,
Laura Godowski
Kevin Jacks
Mike Anderson
Mike Williamson
Payzone Consulting, Inc.

LITHOLOGY
State Gresz 5-26-35H-143-98 Lithology
Rig crews caught samples in 30' intervals from 8,000' to 11,350' and 100' intervals from
11,350' to 20,846' (TD). Formation tops and lithologic markers have been inserted into
the sample descriptions below for reference.
Sample descriptions began in the
Minnelusa Formation. Samples were examined wet and dry under a binocular
microscope and were checked for hydrocarbon cut fluorescence during the lateral.
Hydrocarbon cut was masked by invert mud through 11,331' (intermediate casing) where
the invert mud was exchanged to a saltwater mud for the duration of the lateral.
Quantifiers in order of increasing abundance are trace, rare, occasional, common and
abundant. Subsea is delineated as the negative numbers within the parentheses located
next to the measured depth or true vertical depth. Sample quality was excellent to good.
Overall, the samples within the Middle Bakken target consisted of silty sandstone with
grains that varied from off-white, white, light to medium brown with traces of tan to light
cream, and light grey in color. Siltstone and limestone were present above the top of the
target window. Variances occurred throughout the lateral and are noted below.
Drilling in Minnelusa Formation (Permian; Minnelusa Group)

sub rounded

sub rounded

visible, silty to sandy in part

Dear Leslie:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 20315, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The
approval is granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, be no closer than
the 200' setback from the north & south boundaries and 500' setback from the east & west boundaries within
the 1280 acre spacing unit consisting of Sections 26 & 35, T143N R98W.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Effective June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container (with placard) for
filter sock disposal must be maintained on the well site beginning when the well is spud, and must
remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations are
conducted. OXY USA INC must contact NDIC Field Inspector Nicole Nelson at 701-290-1527 prior to
location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well
drilling and completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will
prevent pollution of the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits
are prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use.
Drill cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings
pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC.
The proposed directional plan is at a legal location. Based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum
legal coordinate from the well head is: 10015'S.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the
approved drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to
commence before the 3rd business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may
be waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information
necessary to evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other
information that would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the
drilling permit, the applicant should retain the permit.
Leslie Teufel Reeves
September 12, 2014
Page 2
Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card .The permit fee has been received. It is requested
that notification be given immediately upon the spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the
Oil & Gas Division, Bismarck, via telephone. The following information must be included: Well name, legal
location, permit number, drilling contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding. Office hours are
8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. and 1:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a
message if after hours or on the weekend.
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor
shall file a certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys
must be submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director may
require the directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the
operation of the director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe
document, with a certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve
(or when sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12
hours, and tail cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi
before drilling the plug or initiating tests.
Logs NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and
(3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation
log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior to completing the well.
All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log
ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to
digitallogs@nd.gov

April 9, 2014
RE:
Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director
State Gresz 5-26-35H-143-98
OXY USA Inc.
